       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/Alma_mater" title="Alma mater">
          Alma mater
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faculdade_de_Direito_da_Universidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Faculdade de Direito da Universidade de São Paulo">
          University of São Paulo
         </a>
         <br/>
         <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Pontifical Catholic University of São Paulo">
          Pontifical Catholic University of São Paulo
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Signature
        </th>
        <td>
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg" title="Michel Temer's signature">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="85" data-file-width="289" height="38" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg/128px-Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg/192px-Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg/256px-Assinatura_Temer_OK.jpg 2x" width="128"/>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Michel Miguel Elias Temer Lulia
       </b>
       (
       <small>
        Portuguese pronunciation:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">
         [miˈʃɛw miˈɡɛw eˈliɐs ˈtemeɾ luˈliɐ]
        </a>
       </span>
       ; born 23 September 1940) is a lawyer and politician who is the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Brazil" title="List of Presidents of Brazil">
        37th
       </a>
       and current
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">
        President of Brazil
       </a>
       . He took office on 31 August 2016 after the
       <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">
        impeachment
       </a>
       and removal from office of his predecessor
       <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">
        Dilma Rousseff
       </a>
       . He had been
       <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Brazil" title="Vice President of Brazil">
        Vice President
       </a>
       since 2011 and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acting_President" title="Acting President">
        Acting President
       </a>
       since 12 May 2016, when Rousseff was suspended while she faced an impeachment trial.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the age of 75, he is the oldest person to have assumed the office.
      </p>
      <p>
       The 31 August 2016 vote of 61–20 meant that Temer succeeded her to serve out the remainder of Rousseff's second term, ending 1 January 2019. In his first speech in office, Temer called for a government of "national salvation" and asked for the trust of the Brazilian people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He also signaled his intention to overhaul the pension system and labor laws, and to curb public spending.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">
        Early life and education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Born in
       <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Tietê, São Paulo">
        Tietê, São Paulo
       </a>
       , Temer is the son of Nakhoul "Miguel" Elias Temer Lulia and March Barbar Lulia,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maronite_Catholic" title="Maronite Catholic">
        Maronite Catholic
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_Brazilian" title="Lebanese Brazilian">
        Lebanese immigrants
       </a>
       who came to Brazil in 1925.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRES_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRES-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His parents, along with three older siblings, immigrated to Brazil from
       <a href="/wiki/Btaaboura" title="Btaaboura">
        Btaaboura
       </a>
       , a small village in northern
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       whose population is entirely
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Antioch" title="Greek Orthodox Church of Antioch">
        Antiochian Greek Orthodox
       </a>
       , to escape
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_of_Mount_Lebanon" title="Great Famine of Mount Lebanon">
        famine
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">
        instability due
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       . In Brazil, his parents had five more children, and Temer is the youngest. Temer is not fluent in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       , but is able to discern the topic of a conversation in that language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_2_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bio_2-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a child, Temer dreamed of becoming a
       <a href="/wiki/Pianist" title="Pianist">
        pianist
       </a>
       . However, there were no piano teachers in his city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a teenager, he wanted to be a writer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After failing chemistry and physics classes in his first year of high school, he gave up the "curso científico", which prioritized hard sciences and math. In 1957, he moved to
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">
        São Paulo
       </a>
       to finish high school in the "curso clássico", composed mainly of subjects in the humanities and languages.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1959, like his four older brothers he joined the
       <a href="/wiki/Law_School,_University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Law School, University of São Paulo">
        Law School of the University of São Paulo
       </a>
       , graduating in 1963.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In his freshman year, he became involved with politics by becoming a treasurer of the school's
       <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">
        students' union
       </a>
       . In 1962, Temer ran for the presidency of the union, but was defeated by 82 votes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Temer stayed neutral before the
       <a href="/wiki/1964_Brazilian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1964 Brazilian coup d'état">
        1964 coup d'état
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the beginning of
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_military_government" title="Brazilian military government">
        military rule
       </a>
       , he moved away from politics. In 1974, he completed a doctorate in
       <a href="/wiki/Public_law" title="Public law">
        public law
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Pontifical Catholic University of São Paulo">
        Pontifical Catholic University of São Paulo
       </a>
       (PUC-SP).
      </p>
      <p>
       Although Temer's parents both hailed from the entirely Antiochian Greek Orthodox village of Btaaboura, he was raised in Brazil within the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
        Catholic
       </a>
       mainstream and has confirmed his affiliation as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.folha.uol.com.br_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-www1.folha.uol.com.br-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_career">
        Academic career
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Academic career">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="2048" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg/150px-Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg/225px-Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg/300px-Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_colar_do_M%C3%A9rito_Judici%C3%A1rio_-_Cortada.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Temer receives the "judicial merit medal"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1968, Temer began teaching
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_law" title="Constitutional law">
        constitutional law
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Pontifical Catholic University of São Paulo">
        PUC-SP
       </a>
       , where he also taught
       <a href="/wiki/Private_law" title="Private law">
        civil law
       </a>
       and was director of the postgraduate department and of the Brazilian Institute Of Constitutional Law as well as a member of the Ibero-American Institute of Constitutional Law.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">
        Publications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Publications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Temer published four major works in constitutional law. His most famous book is
       <i>
        Elements of Constitutional Law
       </i>
       , published in 1982, which sold over 240,000 copies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The book focuses on the organization of the Brazilian state, especially on the
       <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">
        separation of powers
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       His 2006 book
       <i>
        Democracy and Citizenship
       </i>
       highlighted the relevance of law and included some of his speeches as a federal deputy. In his works, he showed himself to be a supporter of
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">
        parliamentarism
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Recall_election" title="Recall election">
        political recall
       </a>
       system, while opposing
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_interventionism" title="Economic interventionism">
        economic interventionism
       </a>
       and tax increases.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, he considered himself a writer only in 2013, when he published
       <i>
        Anonymous Intimacy
       </i>
       , a book of poems. It consists of 120 poems, many of which were written on napkins during his plane trips between São Paulo and
       <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">
        Brasílla
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Temer said writing poems helped him recover from the "barren arena of legislative politics".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_career">
        Political career
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political career">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3826" data-file-width="2313" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg/150px-Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg/225px-Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg/300px-Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vice-presidente_Michel_Temer_com_Medalha_M%C3%A9rito_Legislativo_07.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Michel Temer with the legislative merit medal, which proves his influence in the legislative power.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Beginning in 1987 Temer served six consecutive terms in the
       <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Brazil)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Brazil)">
        Chamber of Deputies
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EC-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and on three separate occasions served two-year terms as president of the Chamber (1997–1998, 1999–2000 and 2009–2010).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRES_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRES-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Temer was also a member of the 1988
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988_Constituent_Assembly" title="1988 Constituent Assembly">
        constituent assembly
       </a>
       , which
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Promulgate" title="Promulgate">
        promulgated
       </a>
       the current
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">
        Constitution of Brazil
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRES_4-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-PRES-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He became President of the
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Democratic_Movement" title="Brazilian Democratic Movement">
        Brazilian Democratic Movement Party
       </a>
       (PMDB), the largest party in Brazil.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-EC-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Temer was the second
       <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Brazil" title="Vice President of Brazil">
        Vice President
       </a>
       of Lebanese origin, after
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Maria_Alkmin" title="José Maria Alkmin">
        José Maria Alkmin
       </a>
       . His family originates from the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Btaaboura" title="Btaaboura">
        Btaaboura
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Koura_District" title="Koura District">
        Koura District
       </a>
       , near
       <a href="/wiki/Tripoli,_Lebanon" title="Tripoli, Lebanon">
        Tripoli
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/North_Governorate" title="North Governorate">
        northern
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Investigations">
        Investigations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Investigations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1250" data-file-width="1250" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg/220px-Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg/330px-Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg/440px-Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_recebe_vice-presidente_norte-americano.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Temer with former
         <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">
          U.S. Vice President
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">
          Joe Biden
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Itamaraty_Palace" title="Itamaraty Palace">
          Itamaraty Palace
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">
          Brasília
         </a>
         , 11 October 2013.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to official government cables published by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikileaks" title="Wikileaks">
        Wikileaks
       </a>
       , Temer provided information to the U.S. Embassy in Brazil in 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Temer is described as gaining the loyalty of lower class Brazilians by strengthening social programs and opposing Lula da Silva.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wikileaks.org_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wikileaks.org-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The report has the status "sensitive but unclassified" with Temer stating that Lula da Silva "might finally begin to heed his friends on the left" and would "be led away from the orthodox macro-economic policies that have dominated his first term".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wikileaks.org_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-wikileaks.org-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_the_impeachment_process_against_Dilma_Rousseff">
        Role in the impeachment process against Dilma Rousseff
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Role in the impeachment process against Dilma Rousseff">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2015 and 2016, Temer was involved in controversy as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impeachment_process_against_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment process against Dilma Rousseff">
        Dilma Rousseff's impeachment process
       </a>
       unfolded. In December 2015, Temer sent a letter to the president complaining about his distance from government decisions. The letter began with the Latin proverb "
       <a href="/wiki/Verba_volant,_scripta_manent" title="Verba volant, scripta manent">
        <i>
         Verba Volant, Scripta Manent
        </i>
       </a>
       " (spoken words fly, written words remain). Temer described the communication as a "personal" unburdening about various complaints against the president. He said Rousseff had made him look like a "decorative" vice president, not an active one, despite having been invited to support her government several times in the dialogue with Congress, a role he only accepted in 2015.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="875" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png/220px-Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png/330px-Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png/440px-Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dilma_Rousseff_Michel_Temer.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Temer campaigning with Dilma Rousseff in 2010.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The letter was commented on and mocked in Brazilian social media, with images depicting the vice president as a Christmas decoration, making fun of his use of Latin, and photos purporting to show the president laughing as she read the missive, among many other things. The president's office had no immediate comment on the images,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but Rousseff condemned him as a traitor to her administration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In April 2016, an audio file of Temer was leaked to the media. In it, Temer speaks as if the impeachment process had already ended and he was the new
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">
        president
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       "I don't want to generate false expectations," Temer said on the recordings, which were first published by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S.Paulo" title="Folha de S.Paulo">
         Folha de S.Paulo
        </a>
       </i>
       on 23 May. "Let's not think that a possible change in government will solve everything in three or four months."
      </p>
      <p>
       The leak came just hours before a special lower house committee was scheduled to vote whether to back the request to impeach the president, generating complaints and accusations of treachery and lack of support from a vice president conspiring against the elected president. Temer alleged it was sent incorrectly to a
       <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">
        WhatsApp
       </a>
       group of his party's representatives in Congress.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_impeachment_attempts">
        First impeachment attempts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First impeachment attempts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_(17316399604).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2090" data-file-width="3139" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_%2817316399604%29.jpg/220px-Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_%2817316399604%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_%2817316399604%29.jpg/330px-Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_%2817316399604%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_%2817316399604%29.jpg/440px-Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_%2817316399604%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presid%C3%AAncia_do_Senado_(17316399604).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
          Eduardo Cunha
         </a>
         (left) at a press conference with fellow PMDB member
         <a href="/wiki/Renan_Calheiros" title="Renan Calheiros">
          Renan Calheiros
         </a>
         (middle) on 21 May 2015.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As investigations following
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">
        Operation Car Wash
       </a>
       grew, allegations against members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Democratic_Movement" title="Brazilian Democratic Movement">
        Brazilian Democratic Movement Party
       </a>
       (PMDB) began to arise. In December 2015, impeachment proceedings toward Temer were filed, though his fellow party member,
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Chamber_of_Deputies_(Brazil)" title="President of the Chamber of Deputies (Brazil)">
        President of the Chamber of Deputies
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
        Eduardo Cunha
       </a>
       , blocked the movement and instead allowed impeachment proceedings against President Rousseff.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VPimpeachment_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-VPimpeachment-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After a Supreme Court judge, Judge Mello, ruled Cunha's actions wrong, he suggested that Temer should face impeachment proceedings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VPimpeachment_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-VPimpeachment-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Another attempt to
       <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_proposals_against_Michel_Temer" title="Impeachment proposals against Michel Temer">
        impeach Temer
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STF_manda_Cunha_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-STF_manda_Cunha-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       began with the decision on 6 April 2016, by the
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Chamber_of_Deputies_(Brazil)" title="President of the Chamber of Deputies (Brazil)">
        president of the Chamber of Deputies
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
        Eduardo Cunha
       </a>
       , to form a commission for termination analysis of liability for crime offered by attorney Mariel M. Marra. Four other requests for impeachment were presented to Cunha.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Cunha, who was third in line for the presidency behind Temer, faced scrutiny for alleged money laundering uncovered in
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">
        Operation Car Wash
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VPimpeachment_24-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-VPimpeachment-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 5 May 2016, Cunha was suspended as speaker of the lower house by Brazil's Supreme Court due to allegations that he attempted to intimidate members of Congress, and obstructed investigations into his alleged receipt of bribes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 17 May 2016, Marcos Aurélio allowed the impeachment request to enter the agenda of the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">
        Supreme Federal Court
       </a>
       plenary session.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_President">
        Acting President
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Acting President">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2444" data-file-width="4131" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg/220px-Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg/330px-Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg/440px-Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Temer_Ministerial_meeting.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Vice President Temer holds his first cabinet meeting as Acting President at the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planalto_Palace" title="Planalto Palace">
          Planalto Palace
         </a>
         , 13 May 2016.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the early hours of 12 May 2016, the Federal Senate voted to accept Rousseff's impeachment and Temer became acting president under the rules set of the Brazilian Constitution, for a maximum of 180 days while the Senate decided whether to convict Rousseff and remove her from office, which would make Temer President for the remainder of her term, or to acquit her of
       <i>
        crimes of responsibility
       </i>
       charges and restore her presidential powers. Temer is awaiting a decision from the Supreme Federal Court to start an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impeachment_proposal_against_Michel_Temer" title="Impeachment proposal against Michel Temer">
        impeachment process against him
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On his first day as acting president, Vice President Temer appointed a new cabinet, reducing the number of ministries from 31 to 22. Women's rights and Afro-Brazilian rights activists criticized the fact that all of the appointed ministers were white men, for the first time since 1979.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 2 June 2016, Temer was declared ineligible to run in the
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_general_election,_2018" title="Brazilian general election, 2018">
        2018 election
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="President_of_Brazil">
        President of Brazil
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: President of Brazil">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section needs to be
          <b>
           updated
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (May 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_(29336546246).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1848" data-file-width="2784" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_%2829336546246%29.jpg/220px-Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_%2829336546246%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_%2829336546246%29.jpg/330px-Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_%2829336546246%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_%2829336546246%29.jpg/440px-Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_%2829336546246%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plen%C3%A1rio_do_Congresso_(29336546246).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Michel Temer during his inauguration in the
         <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">
          National Congress
         </a>
         , 31 August 2016.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2337" data-file-width="3506" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg/220px-Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg/330px-Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg/440px-Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brics_Leaders_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">
          BRICS
         </a>
         leaders in
         <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">
          Hangzhou
         </a>
         , China, 3 September 2016. Left to right: Temer,
         <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">
          Modi
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">
          Xi
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">
          Putin
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">
          Zuma
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Temer succeeded Rousseff as President of Brazil on 31 August 2016. His term finishes on 1 January 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The vice-president position became vacant, and the
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Chamber_of_Deputies_(Brazil)" title="President of the Chamber of Deputies (Brazil)">
        President of the Chamber of Deputies
       </a>
       acts as the first constitutional substitute during his term.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 2016, the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">
        Constitution of Brazil
       </a>
       was amended by deputies
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to cap public spending, effectively frozen for twenty years, adjusted for inflation only. This measure was the subject of both praise and criticism among the Brazilian middle-class.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In November 2016,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Calero" title="Marcelo Calero">
        Marcelo Calero
       </a>
       , Temer's former
       <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Culture_(Brazil)" title="Minister of Culture (Brazil)">
        Minister of Culture
       </a>
       , resigned, stating that Temer had pressured him to help an ally, government secretary
       <a href="/wiki/Geddel_Vieira_Lima" title="Geddel Vieira Lima">
        Geddel Vieira Lima
       </a>
       , who had invested in a development that was being delayed by a heritage preservation measure by allowing construction to go ahead in spite of said measure. Vieira Lima resigned on 25 November 2016, and opposition leaders stated that they would seek President Temer's impeachment over this incident.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Temer denied the corruption allegations but admitted talking to Calero about the project.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2016,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Odebrecht" title="Marcelo Odebrecht">
        Marcelo Odebrecht
       </a>
       confirmed paying bribes to President Temer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 2017, Temer decided to move to the
       <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Jaburu" title="Palácio do Jaburu">
        vice-presidential palace
       </a>
       again. He had recent problems with the Brazilian Historical Heritage Institute due to the architectural changes he made to the
       <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Alvorada" title="Palácio da Alvorada">
        Presidential Palace
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In an interview to the Brazilian news magazine
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Veja_(magazine)" title="Veja (magazine)">
         Veja
        </a>
       </i>
       he mentioned he could not sleep in the "ample rooms" and questioned the possibility of ghosts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 28 April 2017,
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">
        trade unions
       </a>
       called for a
       <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">
        general strike
       </a>
       against the pension and labor reforms proposed in his government,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which failed in many points, especially because the lack of interest of most of the population. Except in state capitals and major cities, in which there were shutdowns of various public services, in most places the strike was restricted to marches, or simply nothing happened
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_impeachment_attempt">
        Second impeachment attempt
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Second impeachment attempt">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 17 May 2017, secretly taped recordings leaked by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/O_Globo" title="O Globo">
         O Globo
        </a>
       </i>
       , a leading national newspaper, reveal the President discussing hush money pay-offs with
       <a href="/wiki/Joesley_Batista" title="Joesley Batista">
        Joesley Batista
       </a>
       , the businessman who runs the country's biggest meat-packing firm
       <a href="/wiki/JBS_S.A." title="JBS S.A.">
        JBS
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       prompting talk of trying again to impeach him.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On Wednesday 24 May 2017, while thousands of angry demonstrators marched towards Congress demanding Temer's resignation and immediate direct presidential elections, President Temer sought to suppress a revolt within his own party.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_(2017-06-20)_04.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1160" data-file-width="1880" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_%282017-06-20%29_04.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_%282017-06-20%29_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_%282017-06-20%29_04.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_%282017-06-20%29_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_%282017-06-20%29_04.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_%282017-06-20%29_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Michel_Temer_(2017-06-20)_04.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         With
         <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">
          Vladimir Putin
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Bolshoi_Theatre" title="Bolshoi Theatre">
          Bolshoi Theatre
         </a>
         in Moscow, 20 June 2017.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Overwhelmed by protests, Temer deployed federal troops to the capital.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many photographs and testimonials taken during the protest show police violence, and officers shooting at demonstrators during the manifestation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       President Temer's refusal to resign is making him increasingly unpopular and has provoked not only a political stalemate but also uncertainty, plunging the country into crisis and amplifying the worst recession in its history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 9 June 2017, the Brazilian
       <a href="/wiki/Superior_Electoral_Court" title="Superior Electoral Court">
        Superior Electoral Court
       </a>
       voted 4–3 to acquit Temer and Rousseff of alleged illegal campaign funding in the 2014 election, thus allowing him to stay in office.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Former Odebrecht Vice President Marcio Faria da Silva said in testimony given as part of a plea bargain that Temer asked him at a meeting to arrange a $40 million payment to Temer's party, the Brazilian Democratic Movement Party (PMDB). Faria said he met with Temer at his law office, and that speaker of the lower house
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Cunha" title="Eduardo Cunha">
        Eduardo Cunha
       </a>
       and Congressman
       <a href="/wiki/Henrique_Eduardo_Alves" title="Henrique Eduardo Alves">
        Henrique Eduardo Alves
       </a>
       were also present. The payment represented a 5% commission on a contract Odebrecht was seeking with the state-run oil company Petrobras, Faria said. Supreme Court Justice Luiz Edson Fachin made this and other testimony public, and ordered an investigation of more than 100 politicians implicated in bribes and kickbacks at state-run companies, particularly Petrobras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_(35796518565).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2337" data-file-width="3506" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_%2835796518565%29.jpg/220px-08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_%2835796518565%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_%2835796518565%29.jpg/330px-08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_%2835796518565%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_%2835796518565%29.jpg/440px-08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_%2835796518565%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:08-07-2017_-_Terceira_Sess%C3%A3o_de_Trabalho_(35796518565).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Temer and
         <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">
          Donald Trump
         </a>
         during the
         <a href="/wiki/2017_G20_Hamburg_summit" title="2017 G20 Hamburg summit">
          12th G20 summit
         </a>
         in Germany, 8 July 2017.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_charges">
        Criminal charges
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Criminal charges">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 26 June 2017, Temer was charged by Prosecutor-General
       <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Janot" title="Rodrigo Janot">
        Rodrigo Janot
       </a>
       with accepting bribes, and Janot delivered the charges to the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">
        Supreme Federal Court
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cnbc-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The lower house must vote on the charges, which stem from allegations that he took $5 million in return for clearing up JBS tax problems and facilitating a loan. Temer still has the support of
       <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Maia" title="Rodrigo Maia">
        Rodrigo Maia
       </a>
       , who replaced Cunha as speaker of the lower house, and has the power to accept or shelve a petition for impeachment. Temer is thought to have the votes to remain in office, but to be vulnerable to a loss of support if repeated votes become necessary. Temer twice changed his justice minister in 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seven_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-seven-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_of_Brazil" title="Federal Police of Brazil">
        Federal Police
       </a>
       (PF) have recommended that Temer also be charged with obstruction of justice.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc_66-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cnbc-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Funding reductions have forced the Federal Police to dismantle the workgroup, leaving some investigations incomplete, and Justice Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Torquato_Jardim" title="Torquato Jardim">
        Torquato Jardim
       </a>
       tried, unsuccessfully, to change PF leadership. A series of legislative initiatives focus on amnesty and changes to the code of criminal procedure.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2017 Temer's approval rating stood at 7%, the lowest for any president in more than thirty years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seven_67-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-seven-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       DataPoder 360 released a poll 21 June which was conducted 19–21 June and showed an approval rating of 2%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In a survey conducted by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IBOPE" title="IBOPE">
        IBOPE
       </a>
       institute between 24 and 26 July 81% of Brazilians favored the indictment of the President.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 2 August, lawmakers in the lower house in Congress voted not to refer the case against the scandal-plagued President to the supreme court, which has the power to try him. Observers and the population state that the move to shield Temer only further undermines the credibility of Brazil's political and electoral system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Deforestation_of_the_Amazon_rainforest">
        Deforestation of the Amazon rainforest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Temer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Deforestation of the Amazon rainforest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 22 August 2017 Temer issued a decree to dissolve the "Reserva Nacional do Cobre e Associados" (Renca)
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">
        Amazonian
       </a>
       reserve in Brazil's northern states of
       <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A1" title="Pará">
        Pará
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amapá">
        Amapá
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After widespread criticism the decree was revoked on 26 September.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_decorations">
        Awards and decorations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Selected awards:
